<gmap_id>0x80c33206fb3939cf:0x6b9bba29df369e1d</gmap_id>< text>
Garfield Park is one of the hard-hitting heartbreaks of Pomona. Driving by at any given time of day, it takes only but a moments glance to fully grasp the visual dissappointment that lingers within the confines of this potential-saturated community recreation area. The lovely overhang coming off the parks tree's cast a summer shade that, sadly, goes unloved by local families and instead is occupied by a number of the cities vagrants, addicts, and drug dealers. (And please, I beg of you, do not mistake my simple-minded observations for a bitter cast of judgement. I try to maintain a non-biased, open minded standard and position; yet to share an opinion, I must either carry a constant dull undertone, or instead speak from the heart.) So, as both a local and a family man, watching this most beautifully manicured and plotted bit of land that could bring a sense of warmth and comfort to a community, centered around the laughter of children and the smell of charcoal through  Autumn nights, and hints of sunscreen in Summer afternoons....day in and day out I see, instead, my minds safe haven tormented by the very bodies that seek shelter within it, and not from weather storms or nature's fury, but from the communities wondering eyes, seeking out the hardened hearts and jaded maids from which society has turned an apathetic eye and blindly guided here. The grass is but a field of landmines in the shapes of broken, dirty syringes and ripped baggy corners, tied and torn balloons, and shattered glass pipes and bottles. The men and woman whom are not the park visiting sort use drugs openly and without shame or merit. Not even an attempt to make themselves unnoticed or inconspicuous to the outside world that borders Garfield. This park is one of my personal raw nerves (I'm sure it's obvious) and on nights that fall too few and far between, when the city empties out, and for a moment the park itself lay still and holds no beating heart, I walk alone through it's somber, silent paths and think, "If only..."<//text>

< text>
Broken Shelf Unit and Missing Mid-Century Lamp--
After examining the Bill of Lading I signed, and the formula to determine our reimbursement (60 cents per pound), it is simply was not worth our time to cover your company's carelessness. We miss our beautiful wooden lamp and our broken shelf unit. I waived the full-value insurance because I truly believed your words when I asked about your movers and the care they would take with our things. That was a risk. The guys you sent to our destination were ridiculous. The move was performed in the dark of night, and before I stopped them, the movers were actually throwing the boxes from the truck to the man on the ground! When I looked in the shuttle truck, everything was strewn across the truck bed, having tumbled over since there were no tie backs used! Even I know how to pack a truck, and I have personally driven our goods across the country without a loss.Shame on me for trusting your words. At the initial pickup point, I even asked the man leading the pickup if you could vouch for the guys on the other end, and I was assured that you "worked with your own people the whole way." Another lesson learned in life I guess.<//text>

< review>
I'm still in the midst of what I hope will be a good resolution to the issues encountered during my move. The packing crew was not professional and did not properly secure some items, while wrapping others directly in duct. AS a consequence, many items arrived damaged and others have duct tape glued on them, that is impossible to remove (glass door of a mini fridge, chrome legs of tables or sofas...).
The delivering crew felt very sorry and apologized. I spoke with Jeff York, the manager, who acknowledged this was not representative of the quality of service provided by his company, and guaranteed I will hear back from Customer Service for compensation. I thought that was reasonable.
The issue is that it's been over 3 weeks. Customer service never reached out to me and Jeff York is now ignoring all my follow up emails. This sounds like they will not own their mistake as they first indicated they would. This is very disappointing. This move was not cheap to start with and, if some issues can arise during a move, I would have expected Jeff and his team to live up to their words and own their mistakes.

Edit: 6 months out now. Jeff at upline never returned any of my calls or emails. Total ghosting. Bringing down the review to 1 star. I would highly recommend you DO NOT hire these movers in the Bay Area. Very nice at first but you are on your own if something goes south (and based on the crew they are hiring, chances are high).<//review>

< review>
Moved about a month ago from CA to east coast. Finally get time to share the review and still hasn't submitted the claim for broken and missing items yet.

Overall if you have nothing valuable, and can pack most things yourself, it might be ok to try this one for the sake of price.
---------------------

One star for excellent pre sales service and update. Was very responsive regarding the request even on Sunday.

One star for the moving cost break down, no hidden cost and reasonable cost.

One star simply for help my family moving during COVID from west coast to east cost. So if this is normal situation, I probably would only give two stars for the move.
--------

Overall I am very disappointed or puzzled by the careless damages/preparation during the transportation, based on my experience of moving about every two years since 2004. And all items damaged/missing were packed by Upline...

1) Told by moving team in CA that customer rep would contact me regarding wall damage (very deep) caused by washing machine. Never happened and still no one contacted me.  And happened again when I told the guy on Monday to confirm delivery as well. Said someone would contact me on Tuesday and never did.
2) One of the child desk legs is completely broken, dangerous for kids to be around.
3) Master bed has one drawer is completely broken. the other drawers can't fit into the bedframe as they were before. The bed slate is damaged with no string connected any more.
4) Garage shelf can't be used due to missing parts for assembly
5) One of the bicycle's tire is completely out of shape. The other two bikes were not assembled due to missing parts.
6)Crib is functioning but damaged with chipped parts

The following two items did not show damage but I am surprised how they are prepared.

7) 34 inch monitor was put in a box with no cushion, wrap or sign with the side edge touch the ground.
8) 40 Gallon fish tank was put in a paper box with side facing down and a metal tool inside the tank.

For comparison, I had way more stuff when I moved to CA and had no issue with any of the items listed above. If it is just one item I can understand, but with so many things, I am hard to believe it happens to an almost 5 start moving company. I am not even picky about there was no mat put on the hardwood floor to prevent any damages during moving or none of the associate wears masks, or I can keep hearing the parts falling on the floor with big bung. Was the crew lack of training or too tired? Or I had wrong expectation on the services at this price range?

Now I am not only need to pay the deductible, but have to go through this tedious claim process. With the Covid, who knows when I will get everything fixed or replaced.

Pretty sure I was told they do not use subcontractor for the long distance delivery but it was not the case. Also got call about 30 min before the driver at my door, and can't get enough cash due to bank closure to pay all by cash...

Not sure it is normal or not, there were only two people unloading on the receiving side. It took more than 10 hours...<//review>

< review>
We have had a terrible experience with Upline, and even if you‚Äôve paid a $50 deposit, I would seriously consider finding a different mover. The one positive about Upline is that the office staff is extremely friendly and responsive. The movers themselves are another story. In short, several of our things are broken irreparably, our TV stand was not (and cannot) be reassembled, a high-end wooden chair was damaged, our computer (shipped in manufacturer‚Äôs packaging) needed repair, and only half of our boxes and furniture were placed in their designated rooms, contrary to Upline‚Äôs marketing promises.

We hired Upline to move our one-bedroom apartment from Oakland, CA to Chicago, IL. We decided to pack our own boxes, and hired Upline to load our things, move them to Chicago, and unload. Upline promised that in Chicago, their movers would unwrap and reassemble furniture and unload boxes and furniture by placing them in whichever room we desired.

In Oakland, the foreman was great, but the movers were pretty roughly handling our stuff; I saw movers toss some of our boxes down the flight of stairs. The Oakland foreman would rein in the movers when he would see them roughly handling our things, but he was busy most of the time executing paperwork with me. So he missed a lot. It‚Äôs no surprise that this handling of our things resulted in a broken lamp and messed up the hardware in the computer that we shipped in manufacturer‚Äôs packaging.

One of the other egregious things I observed is with the loading/packing of our TV stand. I had loaded the cubbies of the TV stand with pillows and a lampshade and taped it off. The movers decided to unload the lampshade, and place it in the bottom of a new box. When I protested, the mover angrily dismissed me, assured me that the lampshade was fine, and then his colleague proceeded to load a laundry basked full of cleaning supplies on top of the lampshade and into the box. It‚Äôs no surprise that the lampshade arrived crushed.

The TV stand didn‚Äôt fare much better. The movers removed the shelves, but did not send the hardware for the shelves to Chicago. They also attempted to disassemble it, but failed, so they packed it with the frame loosely held together. On the Chicago end, the movers could not figure out how to tighten the frame again, and since there was no hardware for the shelves, they didn‚Äôt reinstall the shelves. Now, we can‚Äôt place a TV on the stand because it‚Äôs not sturdy, and we can‚Äôt even use as a bookshelf because there are no shelves.

One of our nicest pieces of furniture was also damaged because the movers did not bother to wrap the legs in a blanket. There is now a large gouge in that piece. These are just some of the highlights of the damage to our things; this is not comprehensive, but you get the idea.

On the Chicago end of our move, the foreman was extremely rude and tried to force me to sign to confirm that individual boxes and pieces of furniture had been delivered, without my seeing the item before signing. When I asked to see each piece before signing for it, he became angry and began to yell at me. I felt extremely uncomfortable.

The Chicago movers themselves (excluding the foreman) were extremely lovely and very carefully handled our furniture. The movers also apologized to me for the foreman‚Äôs behavior. The movers took great care reassembling furniture and made sure they didn‚Äôt damage anything in our building or unit. They began putting boxes and furniture in the designated rooms, but the foreman cleared them out when they were only half done. I didn‚Äôt even have a chance to tip them, so I left a generous tip with the foreman. Who knows if the movers received a cut.

In sum, moving is already stressful, and moving with Upline made things even worse. I‚Äôve filed a complaint with Upline, which was directed to whatever contractor they assign to deal with moving complaints. I will update this post when the claims are resolved.< /review>

< Text>
Helen Wills Park has a lot to offer.  It has basketball courts, a children's playground and play structure, a sandpit for toddlers, and a tennis court all open to the public.  It's funny to see the tennis court (and sometimes the basketball court) covered with chalk drawing that kids doodle during the day.  The tennis court has lights, but currently one of the lights is out and it makes seeing the ball difficult, so be warned!</Text>

<Name>Debra Wilcox<//Name><time>1380579761802< /time><Rating>5<//Rating><Text>This was our neighborhood park for 3 years when living in SF.  Great playground area for the kids, with enough stuff to keep older and younger kids occupied.  There is even a sand box area which is always a hit.
For my older daughter's 2nd bday, we had her party here (on the second level picnic tables).  It worked out perfectly.  Unlike places like Crissy Fields where you have to get down there at the crack of dawn to save a picnic table, we went mid-morning without any issues.  there are public (clean!) bathrooms on site.  Parking is tricky around there though with Polk street right there.  Another nice benefit is even if SF isn't particularly warm, the park gets a lot of sunlight and remains quite warm as its sheltered between buildings.<//Text>< pictures>

<user_id>116792507184480604115</user_id><user_name>Sean Yeske<//user_name><Time>1528358383119</Time>< Rating>
4< /Rating>
< Text>
Dominos is fast food, let's just get that straight.  If you are looking for amazing ingredients, unique recipes or something you have never had before, look elsewhere.  If, however, you are looking for a low cost, decent quality, lightning fast and freshly made lunch or dinner, you've found it.  Definitely use the Domino's app, the coupons alone make it worth the sign-up and the pizza tracker is a bonus.  A personal tip: skip the default "robust inspired tomato sauce" and go for the "hearty marinara".  The tomato sauce is sweet and bland, the marinara contains big pieces of stewed tomatoes and enough spices to make it stand out.  The employees at this location are wonderful.  Fast, friendly and maintain order accuracy.</Text>

< Text>
Kudos for pushing 6-8 cars through the drive-through in about 15 min. This is consistent over a few visits so far. (Kudos for even having a drive-through to begin with and for a location near the I-5 in north county!)  My recent order contained tenders instead of chicken pieces (disappointing for me) and the itemized receipt in my bag was for another person's order (with tenders) instead of showing my own meal deal. The other items in my order were correct though. Probably a simple mix-up. Other recent trips were error-free. They are working very hard to meet high demand and doing quite well, but I hope mix-ups don't become a pattern.  If you're looking for a Popeye's fix, this location is a good solution.< /Text>

We order through drive through, and confirm which sauces we wanted. Drive up window I encountered 3 employees with theirs backs facing me while waiting to be acknowledged for 2-3 minutes.

Get home to enjoy the meal and no SAUCE was provided in our take out. Not that it‚Äôs a big deal but it kinda is because what makes these different from every other place serving fried chicken is there special Louisiana sauces!

If anyone has met an Autistic person you can feel my pain about trying to explain why there is no sauce :( and yes I could have drove back, walked in and complained but I went through drive thru for a reason!

Disappointed special needs Mom</review>

<user_id>115806954984331323487</user_id><Name>David Wolfman<//Name>< Time>
1612215338302< /Time>
<rate>1</rate><Review>There's no such thing as fast food when it comes to any Popeyes that I've ever been to in Southern California; especially this location. This place has lines as long as In-N-Out, and this place is about 3x slower than In-N-Out. Expect to wait 30 to 50 minutes for your order, even without tons of cars in line. Ive gone multiple times because I do love the food and price; however the wait is extremely frustrating and many times I still find myself thinking that it wasnt worth the wait. Don't think that Im being just unreasonable because this location is new...they pulled staff from other Popeyes who were already trained up and it's still unacceptably slow. I dont understand why Popeyes cant keep up with making a lot of food in advance and keeping it warm and fresh (somehow?) in order to keep cars moving through the drive-thru at a much faster pace. KFC can pull off faster cooking so why can't Popeyes? I get that KFC isnt as high quality as Popeyes, but still...there has to be a way for these guys to get orders out faster. If I owned this business I'd be looking into ways to drastically improve production, because it should be clear to any business owner that frustrated customers leads to a decline in repeat sales, and long-lines scare people away, and this means LESS SALES. Popeyes slogan of "Louisiana-Fast" has me thinking the phrase is more of an ironic joke than anything truthful. Louisiana-Fast must mean "half-speed" for the rest of us... Do I expect McDonalds speed? No. But do I expect to wait in line for 50 minutes when there's only 6 cars ahead if me? NO. If great tasting and affordable food is worth it to you and you have no place to be while having no idea how long you'll be stuck in line without being able to quickly leave if youre running low on gas or need to use the restroom...then try it out! It honestly is great food. They really need to fix their production time though; and that's an issue for every local Popeyes around this area. I've been to Popeyes in other states and they're super fast...so maybe its a regional training issue that badly needs attention.</Review>< pictures>
None</pictures>

< Review>
This place has a great location, plenty of parking, and really easy to find, in the heart of Old Town Pasadena. My friend had the strawberry cloudy and I had the Raspberry Cha Latte. Most milk tea shops have boba and other customizable toppings with their drinks, but Cha Redefine focuses on flavor of their teas.

For the pastries, we had the almond croissant and the raspberry Krof'n of Malibu. The croissant was so flaky and crunchy, I wish I ordered one for myself. I know I ordered a raspberry drink and a raspberry pastry, but what can I say? I had a craving for raspberry, and they filled the quota.

If you're in the area, make sure you stop by and try one of their seasonal drinks, you won't be disappointed<//Review>

<Rating>5</Rating><Review>You can't go wrong with The Conservatory. They have fantastic coffee roasted fresh in the shop, their tea selection is insane and the pastry offerings are always on point.
If you need help choosing a coffee, the staff are all very friendly and knowledgable. I've been buying their organic fresh roasted beans for the better part of two years and I can say I have always been greeted with a big smile. Everyone their knows the coffee and can help you decide what beans you'll like based on easy to understand descriptors like "chocolatey" or "fruity." Telling them your brew method of choice isn't a bad idea either.
If you want an intensely fruity, blueberry-like coffee I highly recommend the Ethiopia Yirgacheffe Natural. Ask to smell the beans and you'll be blown away. <Rate>3< /Rate><review>I blindly stopped by Conservatory on a Sunday morning because I needed a place to hang out for an hour before meeting up with a friend nearby. I was surprised to find the line out the door, but since I had an hour to kill I didn't mind that much.

Half an hour later, and I was still waiting in line. There weren't any free tables, and people in line would send other members in their party to sit down before ordering, so that was a bit hopeless. I also didn't realize that there was a separate line for regular coffee because I had spent such a long time outside, so word of advice to anyone just ordering coffee, you can save yourself some time.

Thankfully, I snagged the last zucchini muffin. The cashier serving me snapped it before a large party suggested ordering it, so I was pretty appreciative of her help. It was tasty, but the coffee was underwhelming and they ran out of their regular brew. It was definitely kind of annoying to wait half an hour for things to not be stocked, but oh well.

It's a beautiful space, but given the wait and the average coffee, I likely won't be returning.</review>< Pictures>

< Text>
Okay.. So come during random hours (aka not during the before work or after work times) and you'll land a great spot in front of the place AND no line.

The next thing I wanted to try here was the Mexican mocha latte, but my parched self wanted it cold. And guess what? Ask and you shall receive. I LOVE that this place isn't pretentious. I'm a coffee noon but I love good coffee and the lady who helped me answered all my questions patiently. I wanted to buy a bag of coffee to take home, and she took me to the back of the shop to show me their collection. Wow!!! They have a lot of coffee and tea!!

I love when people have passion for their job and she sure knew her coffee. She was excited to have me smell the coffee beans and the one I chose was from Ethiopia and had a hint of blueberry and you could def smell that from just the beans!

She answered my upkeep questions and I left feeling more educated about coffee! Cool! BTW they grind the coffee according to what brewing device you use... Um awesome!!

Mexican mocha latte was delish cold, but I couldn't tell the difference between that and a mocha latte. I got the Mexican chocolate cookie too.. I could taste the spice there!

If you want to buy the coffee beans/ grounds, they are around $7-8 for half a pound and she said they will last up to 3 weeks in an airtight container<//Text>

<Review>This has been my go to Coffee Shop since I moved to LA in 2010. It has delicious coffee with a casual family vibe that's really nice. I buy my whole bean coffee from them pretty much once a week. They have organic options and everything is roasted fresh, right there in the shop.

The coffee is half the price of most 3rd wave coffee shops (Intelligentsia, Blue Bottle, ETC.) but just as good in my opinion.

The place is family owned and run and all of the barista's and staff are super friendly.

My wife love's Chai Tea Latte's and they make one of the best in town with real tea (not powder) and it's not super sweet like most Chai's. She gets it with the local almond milk that they serve.

We went in for a coffee, two pastries, and a chai the other morning. 11 bucks! It's hard to beat that.

Do yourself a favor and visit the Conservatory the next time you're in the neighborhood.< /Review><Rate>5< /Rate><username>David Whitaker< /username>< Pics>

< review>
I should have tried the coffee, but I didn't. Instead, I got the iced blended vanilla, which was good, but really really sweet. On top of that, I got a chocolate chip cookie, which was also really really sweet, so it was overpowering. Overall, though, this place has an awesome ambience to chill for an hour or so. The tables are a a bit crowded and set to the side and on the front patio. Not a place to get work done. It's too busy, and you would feel bad because no one else is working.

In any case, they have a large selection of coffees and teas, so if you're picky about these things, worth giving it a try. Really easy parking options. You can park on the street itself, or any of the neighborhood side streets have free parking.< /review>

< text>
I'm the 39th review and another person who will 5 star Conservatory.  This is the BEST coffee I've had in LA.  I mostly drink lattes and they do it right.  It's the perfect amount of chocolate mixed with espresso.  I don't get to go every day which is probably good because I really savor getting to go a few times a week.

On Friday I sometimes like to indulge in one of their pastries.  If you're going to go for a muffin I highly suggest the banana chocolate chip.  But, I really like to have a turkey and cheese croissant with my coffee.

In the afternoons you can indulge in a cookie or hot pretzle.  If it's a hot day, I highly suggested an Iced Toffee Latte!<//text>

< review>
I've been coming here for the past 7 years, Whenever I'm visiting family in Rancho Park. Mocha is great, or latte. They roast their own beans. Try the espresso. And get a bag of grains.  Unexpected and welcome business decisions: no junk music, no Wi-Fi. Outside tables (on the sidewalk). Similar in flavor to Long Beach Polly.<//review>
<Gmap_id>0x80c2ba2f308a3f21:0xe6bc11b42dcb0e88<//Gmap_id><pictures>None</pictures><UserId.>104236438121192899522<//UserId.></record></dataset><record>
<response>None< /response><user_id>110291291811378839676</user_id>< Time>
1445123778910< /Time>
< text>
It's all about the beans.

And I suppose the service and the warm, cheerful proprietor and staff, too.

Experience many different tasty varieties of beans.  AJ roasts them fresh on site, and he or his staff can take you through the different options to match your flavor preferences.  Compare to Coffee Bean & Tea Leaf, where the expiration date for the beans is 6 months or more out.  How long has it already been on the shelf?  At the Conservatory, how about roasted TODAY, or yesterday or - say it ain't so! - two or three days ago.  My go-to spot for aa rich,  freshly-brewed cup, or some beans to go for the best espresso at home.

My favorites, when available: Ethiopian Natural (AKA unwashed), and Kenya Peaberry. Lots of other good options, too.</text>
